{{Politics of France}}

[[Legislative elections in France|Legislative election]]s were held in France on 30 June and 7 July 2024 (and one day earlier for some voters outside of metropolitan France) to elect all 577 [[Deputy (France)|members]] of the [[17th legislature of the French Fifth Republic|17th]] [[National Assembly (France)|National Assembly]] of the [[Fifth French Republic]]. The election followed the [[Dissolution of parliament#France|dissolution of the National Assembly]] by President [[Emmanuel Macron]], triggering a [[snap election]] after the [[National Rally]] (RN) made substantial gains and Macron's ''Besoin d'Europe'' [[Party-list proportional representation|electoral list]] lost a significant number of seats in the [[2024 European Parliament election in France|2024 European Parliament election]].<ref>{{Cite web|title=President Emmanuel Macron dissolves French National Assembly and calls snap election|url=https://news.sky.com/story/president-emmanuel-macron-dissolves-french-national-assembly-and-calls-for-snap-election-13150407|access-date=9 June 2024|website=Sky News|language=en|archive-date=28 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240628211113/https://news.sky.com/story/president-emmanuel-macron-dissolves-french-national-assembly-and-calls-for-snap-election-13150407|url-status=live}}</ref>

In the first round of the election, the National Rally and candidates jointly backed by [[Éric Ciotti]] of [[The Republicans (France)|The Republicans]] (LR) led with 33.21%<!-- PLEASE DO NOT CHANGE in accordance with non-official sources: calculated according to the official figures of the Ministry of the Interior, NOT according to the unofficial candidate classifications created by various other media outlets --> of the vote, followed by the parties of the [[New Popular Front]] (NFP) with 28.14%,{{efn|Vote and seat calculations include the following codes assigned by the Ministry of the Interior, corresponding to the alliance or its components: UG, FI, SOC, VEC, and COM. The Ministry of Interior did not report fully disaggregated results by alliance member, with the latter 4 codes only assigned to 11 candidates in total, largely running in either [[Corsica]] or [[overseas France]], of which 7 are categorised by ''Le Monde'' as candidates of the New Popular Front. Because the official candidate classifications of the Ministry of Interior and unofficial classifications of ''Le Monde'' and other sources may differ due to media organisations creating their own candidate classifications, the vote and seat totals reported here may differ from those in other sources. According to ''Le Monde'''s analysis, 182 NFP-affiliated candidates were elected. The seat total here reflects the inclusion of two candidates elected under the SOC code associated with the PS, but is not inclusive of the generic ECO code attributed to miscellaneous ecologist candidates including [[Delphine Batho]] who was officially supported by the New Popular Front, and both this tally and those compiled by other sources may not fully account for all regionalist (REG) or miscellaneous left (DVG) candidates who claim to have the NFP's support, particularly those in [[overseas France]].<ref name="LM1"/><ref name="results2024"/><ref name="LMlive6"/>|name="NFPtotal"}} the pro-Macron alliance [[Together (coalition)|Ensemble]] with 21.28%<!-- PLEASE DO NOT CHANGE, see footnote C: calculated according to the official figures of the Ministry of the Interior, NOT according to the unofficial candidate classifications created by various other media outlets -->,{{efn|Vote and seat calculations include the following codes assigned by the Ministry of the Interior, corresponding to the alliance or its components: ENS, REN, MDM, HOR, and UDI; the latter two codes contain 48 candidates, of which 23 are classified by ''Le Monde'' as being Ensemble candidates. The Ministry of Interior did not report fully disaggregated results by alliance member, and the codes REN and MDM are not applied to any candidates. Because the official candidate classifications of the Ministry of Interior and unofficial classifications of ''Le Monde'' and other sources may differ due to media organisations creating their own candidate classifications, the vote and seat totals reported here may differ from those in other sources.<ref name="LM1"/><ref name="results2024"/> According to ''Le Monde'''s analysis, 168 Ensemble-affiliated candidates were elected.<ref name="LMlive6"/>|name="Etotal"}} and LR candidates with 6.57%,<!-- PLEASE DO NOT CHANGE in accordance with non-official sources: calculated according to the official figures of the Ministry of the Interior, NOT according to the unofficial candidate classifications created by various other media outlets --> with an overall turnout of 66.71%, the highest since [[1997 French legislative election|1997]].<ref name="results2024"/><ref name="Ipsos1997"/> On the basis of these results, a record 306 constituencies were headed to [[Triangular election in France|three-way runoffs]] and 5 to four-way runoffs,<ref name="quadrangulaires">{{cite news|last1=Le Borgne|first1=Brice|title=Résultats des législatives 2024 : record de triangulaires, duels contre le RN... Visualisez les configurations du second tour dans chaque circonscription|url=https://www.francetvinfo.fr/elections/les-cartes-des-legislatives/infographies-resultats-des-legislatives-2024-record-de-triangulaires-duels-contre-le-rn-visualisez-les-configurations-du-second-tour-dans-chaque-circonscription_6631887.html|access-date=1 July 2024|work=franceinfo|archive-date=1 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240701083142/https://www.francetvinfo.fr/elections/les-cartes-des-legislatives/infographies-resultats-des-legislatives-2024-record-de-triangulaires-duels-contre-le-rn-visualisez-les-configurations-du-second-tour-dans-chaque-circonscription_6631887.html|url-status=live}}</ref> but 134 NFP and 82 Ensemble candidates withdrew despite qualifying for the run-off in order to reduce the RN's chances of winning an absolute majority of seats.<ref name="LMwithdrawals"/><ref name="LMlive"/>

In the second round, based on the [[Minister of the Interior (France)|Interior Ministry]]'s candidate labeling, NFP candidates won 180<!-- PLEASE DO NOT CHANGE, see footnote B: calculated according to the official figures of the Ministry of the Interior, NOT according to the unofficial candidate classifications created by various other media outlets --> seats,{{efn|name="NFPtotal"}} with the Ensemble coalition winning 159<!-- PLEASE DO NOT CHANGE, see footnote C: calculated according to the official figures of the Ministry of the Interior, NOT according to the unofficial candidate classifications created by various other media outlets -->,{{efn|name="Etotal"}} National Rally-supported candidates being elected to 142, and LR candidate taking 39 seats. Since no party reached the requisite 289 seats needed for a majority, the second round resulted in a [[hung parliament]]. Unofficial media classifications of candidates' affiliations may differ slightly from those used by the Ministry of Interior: according to ''[[Le Monde]]''{{'}}s analysis, 182 NFP-affiliated candidates were elected, compared with 168 for Ensemble, 143 for the RN, and 45 for LR.<ref name="LMlive6"/><ref name="results2024"/> The turnout for the second round, 66.63%, likewise set the record for being the highest since 1997.

Macron initially refused [[Gabriel Attal]]'s resignation on 8 July, but accepted the resignation of the government on 16 July, allowing ministers to vote for the president of the National Assembly while remaining in place as a caretaker government. NFP leaders called for the appointment of a prime minister from the left, but Ensemble and LR figures advocated for an alliance and threatened that any NFP-led government including ministers from [[La France Insoumise]] (LFI) would face an immediate vote of no confidence. Post-election negotiations between NFP alliance partners exposed renewed tensions, with party leaders taking until 23 July to agree upon a name for prime minister – the 37-year-old director of finance and purchasing for the city of Paris, [[Lucie Castets]]. Macron announced a truce for making political negotiations during the [[2024 Summer Olympics]] on 26 July to 11 August. After the truce, Macron still did not signal any intent to appoint her and called party leaders meeting in Élysée on 23 August, he finally refused to do so on 27 August, leading the NFP to announce they would not take part in further talks with Macron unless it was "to discuss forming a government".<ref>{{Cite news |last=Willsher |first=Kim |date=26 August 2024 |title=Chaos in France after Macron refuses to name prime minister from leftwing coalition |url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/aug/26/chaos-in-france-after-macron-refuses-to-name-prime-minister-from-leftwing-coalition |access-date=27 August 2024 |work=The Guardian |language=en-GB |issn=0261-3077}}</ref>

On 5 September, Macron appointed [[Michel Barnier]] as prime minister. He presented [[Barnier government|his government]] on 19 September and announced on 22 September. On 1 October, Barnier presented his first speech in the National Assembly.<ref>{{Cite news |date=1 October 2024 |title= 5 things to watch for in French PM Barnier’s first parliamentary address |url= https://www.politico.eu/article/michel-barnier-big-day-lawmakers-speech-france-coalition-government-debt-tax-rate-migration-labor/ |access-date=1 October 2024 |language=en-GB}}</ref> Analysts noted that the failure of any bloc to attain support from an absolute majority of deputies could lead to institutional deadlock because any government must be able to survive [[motion of no confidence|motions of no confidence]] against them. Although Macron can call a second snap election, he is unable to do so until at least a year after the 2024 election, as stipulated by the [[constitution of France|constitution]]. On 9 October, Barnier survived a motion of no confidence led by 193 members of the NFP and 4 members of LIOT members support.{{Citation needed|date=October 2024}} Another motion of no confidence, led by the National Rally and the leftist coalition on 4 December, successfully ousted Barnier with 331 votes in favor.<ref>{{Cite news |date=4 December 2024 |title= France’s Prime Minister Loses No-Confidence Vote and Is Expected to Resign |url= https://www.nytimes.com/2024/12/04/world/europe/france-no-confidence-barnier.html |access-date=4 December 2024 |language=en-US}}</ref>

==Background==
Following the [[2022 French legislative election|2022 legislative election]], [[Together (coalition)|Ensemble]] lost its [[absolute majority]] in the [[National Assembly (France)|National Assembly]]. Among the member parties of the coalition was President [[Emmanuel Macron]]'s party, [[Renaissance (French political party)|Renaissance]] (formerly La République En Marche!). Meanwhile, the two main opposition blocs, the left-wing [[New Ecological and Social People's Union]] (NUPES) and far-right [[National Rally]] (RN) made significant gains in terms of seats. Despite that, no group won the absolute majority, resulting in a [[hung parliament]] for the first time since the [[1988 French legislative election|1988 election]].<ref>{{Cite web|last=Bernard|first=Mathias|title=Parliamentary elections shock France's political order to its core|url=https://theconversation.com/parliamentary-elections-shock-frances-political-order-to-its-core-185413|access-date=17 June 2024|website=The Conversation|date=20 June 2022|language=en|archive-date=20 June 2022|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20220620145616/http://theconversation.com/parliamentary-elections-shock-frances-political-order-to-its-core-185413|url-status=live}}</ref> The lack of an absolute majority led to the repeated invocation of [[article 49 of the French Constitution#Commitment of responsibility on a bill (49.3)|article 49.3]] of the constitution in order to adopt legislation, with [[Élisabeth Borne]] doing so 23 times by December 2023.<ref>{{cite news|title=Elisabeth Borne utilise l'article 49.3 pour la 23e fois de la législature|url=https://www.liberation.fr/politique/elisabeth-borne-utilise-larticle-493-pour-la-23e-fois-de-la-legislature-20231219_AWQGDOD7L5CB5OQ2ROID7PCCPE/|access-date=25 June 2024|work=Libération|agency=Agence France-Presse|date=19 December 2023|archive-date=3 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240603215815/https://www.liberation.fr/politique/elisabeth-borne-utilise-larticle-493-pour-la-23e-fois-de-la-legislature-20231219_AWQGDOD7L5CB5OQ2ROID7PCCPE/|url-status=live}}</ref>

On 9 June 2024, shortly after 21:00 CEST, Macron [[Dissolution of parliament#France|dissolved]] the National Assembly and called [[snap election]]s in a national address following projections which indicated that the [[L'Europe Ensemble]] [[Party-list proportional representation|electoral list]] would be significantly eclipsed by the RN in the [[2024 European Parliament election in France|European Parliament elections in France]]. In his address, he called the rise of nationalism by agitators a threat to France, Europe, and France's place in the world. He also warned that the far-right would bring about the "impoverishment of the French people and the downfall of our country." The dates of the first and second rounds of elections were set for 30 June and 7 July, respectively.<ref name=":3">{{Cite web|date=9 June 2024|title=French President Macron dissolves parliament, calls snap elections|url=https://www.euronews.com/my-europe/2024/06/09/french-president-emmanuel-macron-announces-anticipated-elections-after-stinging-eu-electio|access-date=9 June 2024|website=euronews|language=en|archive-date=9 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240609194328/https://www.euronews.com/my-europe/2024/06/09/french-president-emmanuel-macron-announces-anticipated-elections-after-stinging-eu-electio|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Reactions to the announcement===

====Politicians====
RN leader [[Jordan Bardella]] called the large gap between the RN and L'Europe Ensemble electoral lists in the European Parliament elections a "stinging disavowal" of President Macron, saying that the results marked "day 1 of the post-Macron era."<ref>{{Cite web|last1=Kennedy|first1=Niamh|last2=Edwards|first2=Christian|date=9 June 2024|title=Macron calls snap parliamentary election after crushing loss to far-right in European election poll|url=https://www.cnn.com/2024/06/09/europe/macron-dissolves-french-parliament-europe-intl/index.html|access-date=9 June 2024|website=CNN|language=en|archive-date=9 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240609203053/https://www.cnn.com/2024/06/09/europe/macron-dissolves-french-parliament-europe-intl/index.html|url-status=live}}</ref> [[Marine Le Pen]], president of the RN group in the National Assembly, and [[Jean-Luc Mélenchon]], leader of [[La France Insoumise]], celebrated the election results and welcomed the announcement of [[snap election]]s.<ref name=":3"/>

Former president [[Nicolas Sarkozy]] condemned Macron, seeing his decision to dissolve parliament as a "serious risk for the country."<ref>{{cite news|last1=Lejeune|first1=Geoffroy|last2=André|first2=Antonin|title=EXCLUSIF – Nicolas Sarkozy au JDD : " La dissolution constitue un risque majeur pour le pays "|url=https://www.lejdd.fr/politique/exclusif-nicolas-sarkozy-au-jdd-la-dissolution-constitue-un-risque-majeur-pour-le-pays-146419|access-date=28 June 2024|work=Le Journal du Dimanche|date=15 June 2024|archive-date=28 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240628105735/https://www.lejdd.fr/politique/exclusif-nicolas-sarkozy-au-jdd-la-dissolution-constitue-un-risque-majeur-pour-le-pays-146419|url-status=live}}</ref> Mayor of Paris [[Anne Hidalgo]] reacted extremely negatively to Macron's decision, saying that the elections posed a serious threat to the upcoming [[2024 Summer Olympics]] because they would not only "spoil the mood of the whole country" but also carry the risk of street riots and demonstrations.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Ngendakumana|first1=Pierre Emmanuel|title=Macron 'spoiled the party' by calling snap vote before the Olympics, Paris Mayor Anne Hidalgo says|url=https://www.politico.eu/article/france-emmanuel-macron-olympics-snap-election-paris-anne-hidalgo/|access-date=28 June 2024|work=Politico Europe|date=26 June 2024|archive-date=28 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240628124000/https://www.politico.eu/article/france-emmanuel-macron-olympics-snap-election-paris-anne-hidalgo/|url-status=live}}</ref>

====Media====
The decision to hold an election came as a surprise to outside observers and was widely seen as being risky for the presidential majority of Emmanuel Macron, with some suggesting that Macron wished to force a decision between the RN and their opposition and others assessing that Macron intended to win a majority,<ref>{{cite web|last=Henley|first=Jon|title=Three possible outcomes of Macron's shocking snap election|website=the Guardian|date=10 June 2024|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/jun/10/three-possible-outcomes-of-macrons-shocking-snap-election|access-date=11 June 2024|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630225605/https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/jun/10/three-possible-outcomes-of-macrons-shocking-snap-election|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite web|last1=Jones|first1=Sam|last2=Henley|first2=Jon|last3=Rankin|first3=Jennifer|last4=O'Carroll|first4=Lisa|title=French parties hold emergency talks with possible allies for snap election|website=the Guardian|date=10 June 2024|url=https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/jun/10/france-braced-election-far-right-surge-macron|access-date=11 June 2024|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630225606/https://www.theguardian.com/world/article/2024/jun/10/france-braced-election-far-right-surge-macron|url-status=live}}</ref> with Renaissance leader [[Stéphane Séjourné]] attempting to tempt moderate incumbents on both the left and right to join his alliance in comments made just after the dissolution was announced.<ref name="Sejourne">{{cite news|title=Législatives anticipées : "On commence ce matin une campagne, rien n'est joué, ce sera projet contre projet", assure Clément Beaune|url=https://www.francetvinfo.fr/politique/parlement-francais/assemblee-nationale/dissolution/legislatives-anticipees-on-commence-ce-matin-une-campagne-rien-n-est-joue-ce-sera-projet-contre-projet-assure-clement-beaune_6595692.html|access-date=25 June 2024|work=franceinfo|date=10 June 2024|archive-date=25 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240625065912/https://www.francetvinfo.fr/politique/parlement-francais/assemblee-nationale/dissolution/legislatives-anticipees-on-commence-ce-matin-une-campagne-rien-n-est-joue-ce-sera-projet-contre-projet-assure-clement-beaune_6595692.html|url-status=live}}</ref>

Most international media expressed deep surprise at Macron's decision, calling the snap elections a "desperate gamble." In general, Macron's decision was perceived negatively, and the prospects for his alliance's victory in the elections were assessed as low. ''[[La Libre Belgique]]'' called Macron a "wounded political animal."<ref>{{cite news|last1=Durieux|first1=Jeanne|title=Dissolution de l'Assemblée : la presse étrangère sceptique et sévère face au "pari fou" d'Emmanuel Macron|url=https://www.lefigaro.fr/politique/dissolution-de-l-assemblee-la-presse-etrangere-sceptique-et-severe-face-au-pari-fou-d-emmanuel-macron-20240610|access-date=28 June 2024|work=Le Figaro|date=10 June 2024|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630225606/https://www.lefigaro.fr/politique/dissolution-de-l-assemblee-la-presse-etrangere-sceptique-et-severe-face-au-pari-fou-d-emmanuel-macron-20240610|url-status=live}}</ref> According to the [[BBC]], by calling snap elections, Macron jeopardised the democracy of the [[French Fifth Republic|Fifth Republic]] and risked provoking violence in the streets and institutional collapse.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Schofield|first1=Hugh|title=Macron's election gamble puts French democracy on the table|url=https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cekk9n1je9yo|access-date=28 June 2024|work=BBC News|date=25 June 2024|archive-date=28 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240628122638/https://www.bbc.com/news/articles/cekk9n1je9yo|url-status=live}}</ref> ''[[The Guardian]]'' considered Macron's measures an attempt to avenge his defeat in the preceding European Parliament elections, which could result in radicals coming to power and splitting the country.<ref>{{cite news|title=The Guardian view on Macron's snap election: France on the brink|url=https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/article/2024/jun/24/the-guardian-view-on-macrons-snap-election-france-on-the-brink|access-date=28 June 2024|work=The Guardian|date=24 June 2024|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630221146/https://www.theguardian.com/commentisfree/article/2024/jun/24/the-guardian-view-on-macrons-snap-election-france-on-the-brink|url-status=live}}</ref> ''[[Die Zeit]]'' believed that Macron "lost his cool" to such an extent that he actually "gave the country to Marine Le Pen." The Greek daily newspaper ''[[Kathimerini]]'' called Macron's decision an unwise gamble that would lead to nothing good.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Katsikidis|first1=Athanasios|title=Lequesne: 'Macron is putting democracy at risk'|url=https://www.ekathimerini.com/politics/foreign-policy/1242458/lequesne-macron-is-putting-democracy-at-risk/|access-date=28 June 2024|work=Ekathimerini|date=26 June 2024|archive-date=28 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240628014802/https://www.ekathimerini.com/politics/foreign-policy/1242458/lequesne-macron-is-putting-democracy-at-risk/|url-status=live}}</ref> French media raised the issue of holding the 2024 Summer Olympics in conditions of political instability.<ref>{{cite news|title=Paris mayor slams Macron's election call before Olympics|url=https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20240610-paris-mayor-slams-macron-s-election-call-before-olympics|access-date=28 June 2024|work=France 24|agency=Agence France-Presse|date=10 June 2024|archive-date=28 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240628124005/https://www.france24.com/en/live-news/20240610-paris-mayor-slams-macron-s-election-call-before-olympics|url-status=live}}</ref>

==Electoral system==
{{Bar box
|float=left
|title=Constituencies with three- or four-way runoffs<br/>(before candidate withdrawals)<ref>{{cite news|last1=Mainguet|first1=Maxime|last2=Qi|first2=Yiping|title=Législatives 2024 : pourquoi le nombre de triangulaires s'annonce très important|url=https://cholet.maville.com/actu/actudet_-legislatives-2024-pourquoi-le-nombre-de-triangulaires-s-annonce-tres-important-_54135-6357437_actu.Htm|access-date=28 June 2024|work=Ouest-France|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630205851/https://cholet.maville.com/actu/actudet_-legislatives-2024-pourquoi-le-nombre-de-triangulaires-s-annonce-tres-important-_54135-6357437_actu.Htm|url-status=live}}</ref><ref>{{cite news|last1=Chambraud|first1=Cécile|title=Soixante-seize triangulaires en présence de l'extrême droite|url=https://www.lemonde.fr/archives/article/1997/05/29/soixante-seize-triangulaires-en-presence-de-l-extreme-droite_3762441_1819218.html|access-date=28 June 2024|work=Le Monde|date=29 May 1997|archive-date=24 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240624200600/https://www.lemonde.fr/archives/article/1997/05/29/soixante-seize-triangulaires-en-presence-de-l-extreme-droite_3762441_1819218.html|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="quadrangulaires"/>
|left1=Year
|bars=
{{bar pixel|[[1988 French legislative election|1988]]|blue|2.75||11}}
{{bar pixel|[[1993 French legislative election|1993]]|blue|3.75||15}}
{{bar pixel|[[1997 French legislative election|1997]]|blue|19.75||105}}
{{bar pixel|[[2002 French legislative election|2002]]|blue|2.5||10}}
{{bar pixel|[[2007 French legislative election|2007]]|blue|0.25||1}}
{{bar pixel|[[2012 French legislative election|2012]]|blue|11.5||46}}
{{bar pixel|[[2017 French legislative election|2017]]|blue|0.25||1}}
{{bar pixel|[[2022 French legislative election|2022]]|blue|2||8}}
{{bar pixel|'''2024'''|blue|78.25||311}}

The 577 members of the [[National Assembly (France)|National Assembly]], known as [[Member of Parliament (France)|deputies]], are elected for five years by a [[two-round system]] in single-member [[List of constituencies of the National Assembly of France|constituencies]]. A candidate who receives an absolute majority of valid votes and a vote total greater than 25% of the registered electorate is elected in the first round. If no candidate reaches this threshold, a runoff election is held between the top two candidates plus any other candidate who received a vote total greater than 12.5% of registered voters. The candidate who receives the most votes in the second round is elected.<ref>{{cite web|url=https://www.electionguide.org/elections/id/2570/|url-status=live|title=Elections: France National Assembly 2017 (first round)|website=Election Guide|publisher=International Foundation for Electoral Systems|date=11 June 2017|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20200815164019/https://www.electionguide.org/elections/id/2570/|archive-date=15 August 2020|access-date=16 June 2022}}</ref>

A consequence of the 12.5% threshold was the potential for [[three-cornered-contest|three-way runoffs]], also referred to as [[Triangular election in France|triangular elections]], in a greater number of constituencies in the second round in the event of higher turnout and diminished number of candidates, as was anticipated to be the case in 2024 relative to previous legislative elections. Such a dynamic reinforced the likelihood that higher turnout became an advantage for the [[National Rally]], which received a clear plurality of the vote in pre-first round polls and as a result would be expected to win a greater share of seats due to the increased number of three-way races in the second round, not accounting for the possibility of candidate withdrawals.<ref>{{cite web|title=Forte participation, triangulaires en masse, RN à portée de majorité absolue, NFP en progression et Renaissance en chute libre|url=https://www.odoxa.fr/sondage/13142-2/|publisher=Odoxa|access-date=21 June 2024|date=21 June 2024|archive-date=24 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240624165632/https://www.odoxa.fr/sondage/13142-2/|url-status=live}}</ref>

With pre-election polls suggesting that the 2024 legislative elections would feature the highest level of turnout in decades with an exceptionally tripolarised electorate, pre-election estimates of the potential number of three-way races were also at unprecedented levels,<ref name="Ipsos300">{{cite news|title=Législatives 2024 : vers un nombre record de triangulaires à l'issue du premier tour|url=https://www.leparisien.fr/elections/legislatives/legislatives-2024-vers-un-nombre-record-de-triangulaires-a-lissue-du-premier-tour-30-06-2024-VF5REUFN6ZGVVO6A6FO7BJEO34.php|access-date=30 June 2024|work=Le Parisien|date=30 June 2024|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630205848/https://www.leparisien.fr/elections/legislatives/legislatives-2024-vers-un-nombre-record-de-triangulaires-a-lissue-du-premier-tour-30-06-2024-VF5REUFN6ZGVVO6A6FO7BJEO34.php|url-status=live}}</ref> and ultimately 306 constituencies headed to three-way runoffs and 5 to four-way runoffs,<ref name="quadrangulaires"/> with 89 three-way and 2 four-way runoffs remaining after candidate withdrawals announced ahead of the registration deadline for the second round.<ref name="LMwithdrawals"/> This marked the first time since [[1973 French legislative election|1973]] that four-way runoffs, also referred to as ''quadrangulaires'', were necessary in any [[Legislative elections in France|French legislative election]].<ref name="q1973">{{cite news|last1=Hazo|first1=Josselin|title=Législatives : des quadrangulaires vont se disputer dimanche, du jamais-vu depuis 1973|url=https://www.leparisien.fr/elections/legislatives/legislatives-des-quadrangulaires-vont-se-disputer-dimanche-du-jamais-vu-depuis-1973-03-07-2024-MRSEVLFPTNEVPHMCCDPHQD46VI.php|access-date=4 July 2024|work=Le Parisien|date=3 July 2024|archive-date=3 July 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240703194635/https://www.leparisien.fr/elections/legislatives/legislatives-des-quadrangulaires-vont-se-disputer-dimanche-du-jamais-vu-depuis-1973-03-07-2024-MRSEVLFPTNEVPHMCCDPHQD46VI.php|url-status=live}}</ref>

==Campaign==

===Timeline===
The two rounds of the election were held on 30 June and 7 July in [[metropolitan France]] (France, adjacent islands, [[Corsica]]), while each round took place a day earlier in France's overseas [[French departments|departments]] ([[Saint Pierre and Miquelon]], [[Saint Barthélemy]], [[Collectivity of Saint Martin|Saint Martin]], [[Guadeloupe]], [[Martinique]], [[French Guiana]], [[French Polynesia]]) as well as in embassies and consular posts in the [[Americas]]. Polling stations were open from 8:00 to 18:00 local time, with some open until 20:00.<ref>{{cite web|title=Législatives 2024 : le décret de convocation des électeurs est paru|url=https://www.vie-publique.fr/en-bref/294573-legislatives-2024-le-decret-de-convocation-des-electeurs-est-paru|publisher=Vie publique|access-date=29 June 2024|date=10 June 2024|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630212422/https://www.vie-publique.fr/en-bref/294573-legislatives-2024-le-decret-de-convocation-des-electeurs-est-paru|url-status=live}}</ref> All media coverage in terms of candidate interviews and programmes, campaigning, and publication of public opinion polls were banned from midnight on the day before the election in (29 June and 6 July) to the closing of the last polling stations on election day.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Groult|first1=Arthur|title=Elections législatives : pourquoi le débat politique est-il interdit en France à la veille du scrutin ?|url=https://www.ladepeche.fr/2024/06/29/elections-legislatives-pourquoi-le-debat-politique-est-il-interdit-en-france-a-la-veille-du-scrutin-12049236.php|access-date=29 June 2024|work=La Dépêche|date=29 June 2024|archive-date=29 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240629180815/https://www.ladepeche.fr/2024/06/29/elections-legislatives-pourquoi-le-debat-politique-est-il-interdit-en-france-a-la-veille-du-scrutin-12049236.php|url-status=live}}</ref>

The timeline for candidates to register for the first round of elections was from 12 June until 16 June, while the candidate registration deadline for the second round is 2 July.<ref>{{cite web|title=What are the rules for France's snap parliamentary elections?|website=Le Monde|date=13 June 2024|url=https://www.lemonde.fr/en/politics/article/2024/06/13/what-will-be-the-rules-of-france-s-snap-parliamentary-elections_6674633_5.html|access-date=15 June 2024|last=Cosnard|first=Denis|archive-date=15 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240615171742/https://www.lemonde.fr/en/politics/article/2024/06/13/what-will-be-the-rules-of-france-s-snap-parliamentary-elections_6674633_5.html|url-status=live}}</ref> The official campaign, during which audio-visual and electoral regulations must be respected, began on 17 June.<ref>{{Cite news|date=14 June 2024|title=France kicks off accelerated campaign after Macron's legislative poll gamble|url=https://www.france24.com/en/france/20240617-france-kicks-off-accelerated-campaign-after-macron-s-legislative-poll-gamble|access-date=17 June 2024|website=France 24|language=en|archive-date=20 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240620213621/https://www.france24.com/en/france/20240617-france-kicks-off-accelerated-campaign-after-macron-s-legislative-poll-gamble|url-status=live}}</ref>

For those registered on consular electoral lists, online voting for [[constituencies for French residents overseas]] ran from 25 June at 12:00 CEST to 27 June at 12:00 CEST for the first round, and from 3 July at 12:00 CEST to 4 July at 18:00 CEST for the second round. Many of those attempting to vote on 25 June reported that the voting website was unreachable due to high traffic.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Leroy|first1=Thomas|title=Législatives: à peine ouvert, le portail de vote en ligne pour les Français de l'étranger rencontre des difficultés|url=https://www.bfmtv.com/tech/vie-numerique/legislatives-a-peine-ouvert-le-portail-de-vote-en-ligne-pour-les-francais-de-l-etranger-deja-sature_AV-202406250547.html|access-date=25 June 2024|work=BFMTV|date=25 June 2024|archive-date=25 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240625122107/https://www.bfmtv.com/tech/vie-numerique/legislatives-a-peine-ouvert-le-portail-de-vote-en-ligne-pour-les-francais-de-l-etranger-deja-sature_AV-202406250547.html|url-status=live}}</ref> The [[Ministry for Europe and Foreign Affairs (France)|Ministry for Foreign Affairs]] announced on 27 June that 410,000 online ballots were cast during the voting period, a new record compared to 250,000 in 2022.<ref>{{cite news|title=Elections législatives 2024 : participation record pour les Français de l'étranger, avec 410 000 votants sur internet|url=https://www.francetvinfo.fr/elections/legislatives/legislatives-2024-participation-record-pour-les-francais-de-l-etranger-avec-410-000-votants-sur-internet_6629907.html|access-date=30 June 2024|work=franceinfo|agency=Agence France-Presse|date=27 June 2024|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630022223/https://www.francetvinfo.fr/elections/legislatives/legislatives-2024-participation-record-pour-les-francais-de-l-etranger-avec-410-000-votants-sur-internet_6629907.html|url-status=live}}</ref>

The extremely short amount of time to prepare for the election posed significant logistical challenges, especially in [[overseas France]], due to municipalities being required to cover the costs of organising the ballot by themselves in addition to the necessity of recruiting and training volunteers to run polling stations in relatively little time.<ref>{{cite news|title=Législatives 2024. Le casse-tête de l'organisation|url=https://la1ere.francetvinfo.fr/elections-legislatives-2024-le-casse-tete-de-l-organisation-1496888.html|access-date=25 June 2024|work=Outre-mer la 1ère|date=14 June 2024|archive-date=25 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240625082636/https://la1ere.francetvinfo.fr/elections-legislatives-2024-le-casse-tete-de-l-organisation-1496888.html|url-status=live}}</ref> In a press release, the {{ill|Association of Mayors of France|fr|Association des maires de France}} stated that many mayors remained worried "about the ability of their communes to organise these two elections under satisfactory conditions." While monetary compensation for assessors is usually prohibited, some communes opted to ignore the electoral code given that exceptions were granted to communes under similarly "exceptional circumstances" in the past. Furthermore, the timing of the election made it impossible for candidates and parties to present enough representatives presents at polling stations, with only a tenth of those required having been nominated in [[Nice]]. While such issues might normally be sufficient reason for the [[Constitutional Council (France)|Constitutional Council]] to annul election results in specific constituencies, legal scholars considered this possibility unlikely given the lack of time for officials to prepare for the elections.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Hélin|first1=Lucas|title=Législatives : en manque d'assesseurs dans ses bureaux de vote, la mairie de Nice veut attirer les candidats avec une rémunération|url=https://www.lefigaro.fr/nice/legislatives-en-manque-d-assesseurs-dans-ses-bureaux-de-vote-la-mairie-de-nice-veut-attirer-les-candidats-avec-une-remuneration-20240625|access-date=27 June 2024|work=Le Figaro|date=25 June 2024|archive-date=26 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240626130212/https://www.lefigaro.fr/nice/legislatives-en-manque-d-assesseurs-dans-ses-bureaux-de-vote-la-mairie-de-nice-veut-attirer-les-candidats-avec-une-remuneration-20240625|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Protests===
[[File:Manif reims anti fascisme 1523908.jpg|thumb|upright=1.5|Protests against the far-right in [[Reims]] on 14 June]]
{{Main article|2024 French protests against the far-right}}
On 9 June 2024, protests started immediately following the European election results, where several hundred people demonstrated against the RN's victory at [[Place de la République]] in [[Paris]] and called for a "union of the left" in the next legislative elections and several dozen people chanting anti-[[Jordan Bardella]] slogans in [[Lille]].<ref>{{Cite AV media|url=https://www.ouest-france.fr/elections/europeennes/video-europeennes-plusieurs-centaines-de-personnes-place-de-la-republique-a-paris-contre-le-rn-b3182cc2-575a-4dc0-99ce-047600067f7f|title=Vidéo. Européennes : plusieurs centaines de personnes place de la République à Paris contre le RN|date=10 June 2024|language=fr|access-date=25 June 2024|via=www.ouest-france.fr|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630211349/https://www.ouest-france.fr/elections/europeennes/video-europeennes-plusieurs-centaines-de-personnes-place-de-la-republique-a-paris-contre-le-rn-b3182cc2-575a-4dc0-99ce-047600067f7f|url-status=live}}</ref> Many [[Trade union|labour unions]], [[Student society|student groups]], [[human rights group]]s, and political parties called for rallies in order to oppose the [[Opposition to immigration|anti-immigration]] and [[Euroscepticism|Eurosceptic]] policies of National Rally, and to promote "[[Progressivism|progressive]] alternatives for the world of work".<ref>{{Cite news|last1=Kim|first1=Juliana|last2=Bowman|first2=Emma|date=15 June 2024|title=French protesters turn out to oppose far-right shift ahead of snap election|url=https://www.npr.org/2024/06/15/nx-s1-5007391/french-protests-oppose-far-right-election|access-date=25 June 2024|work=NPR|archive-date=26 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240626004442/https://www.npr.org/2024/06/15/nx-s1-5007391/french-protests-oppose-far-right-election|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name=":3c">{{Cite web|date=11 June 2024|title=Nantes : un drapeau français arraché à une fenêtre en marge d'une manifestation anti-RN|url=https://www.lejdd.fr/politique/nantes-un-drapeau-francais-arrache-une-fenetre-en-marge-dune-manifestation-anti-rn-146234|access-date=25 June 2024|website=lejdd.fr|language=fr|archive-date=30 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240630210408/https://www.lejdd.fr/politique/nantes-un-drapeau-francais-arrache-une-fenetre-en-marge-dune-manifestation-anti-rn-146234|url-status=live}}</ref> Political parties that called for rallies included the [[Socialist Party (France)|Socialist Party]], [[French Communist Party|Communist Party]], [[The Ecologists (political party)|The Ecologists]] and [[La France Insoumise]], while union groups calling for rallies included the [[French Democratic Confederation of Labour]] (CFDT), the [[General Confederation of Labour (France)|General Confederation of Labour]] (CGT), the [[National Union of Autonomous Trade Unions]] (UNSA), the [[Fédération Syndicale Unitaire]] (FSU), and the [[Union syndicale Solidaires|Solidaires]], promoting the "largest possible" demonstrations.<ref name=":3c"/>

On 18 June, the CGT called for voters to support the left-of-centre [[New Popular Front]] alliance, marking the first time it ever issued specific voting instructions for a specific candidate or party.<ref>{{cite news|last1=Kagni|first1=Maxence|title=Législatives : la CGT appelle à voter pour le Nouveau Front populaire, que disent les autres syndicats et les organisations patronales ?|url=https://lcp.fr/actualites/legislatives-la-cgt-appelle-a-voter-pour-le-nouveau-front-populaire-que-disent-les|access-date=26 June 2024|work=LCP-Assemblée nationale|date=19 June 2024|archive-date=28 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240628132835/https://lcp.fr/actualites/legislatives-la-cgt-appelle-a-voter-pour-le-nouveau-front-populaire-que-disent-les|url-status=live}}</ref>

===Parties and coalitions===

====Summary====
Below are the major parties and alliances (including any primary components with candidates in at least 3 constituencies) contesting the elections in a majority (289 or more as tallied by ''[[Le Monde]]'') of constituencies, listed by their combined results in the previous elections.<ref name="LM1">{{cite news|last1=Sanchez|first1=Léa|last2=Derœux|first2=Iris|last3=Pateman|first3=Lili|last4=Parienté|first4=Jonathan|last5=Audureau|first5=William|last6=Imbach|first6=Romain|last7=Tovo|first7=Françoise|last8=Durand|first8=Anne-Aël|last9=Breteau|first9=Pierre|last10=Leloup|first10=Damien|last11=Baruch|first11=Jérémie|last12=Ferrer|first12=Maxime|title=Découvrez la liste des candidats aux élections législatives 2024 dans votre circonscription|url=https://www.lemonde.fr/les-decodeurs/article/2024/06/19/qui-sont-les-candidats-aux-elections-legislatives-2024-decouvrez-la-liste-circonscription-par-circonscription_6241357_4355770.html|access-date=21 June 2024|work=Le Monde|date=19 June 2024|archive-date=21 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240621045056/https://www.lemonde.fr/les-decodeurs/article/2024/06/19/qui-sont-les-candidats-aux-elections-legislatives-2024-decouvrez-la-liste-circonscription-par-circonscription_6241357_4355770.html|url-status=live}} Footnotes using this reference may also make use of [[JSON]] data [https://assets-decodeurs.lemonde.fr/sheets/0MYjaeDiKHgpmFRAtpks9CpOuqkX-g_2888 embedded] ({{Webarchive|url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240621173458/https://assets-decodeurs.lemonde.fr/sheets/0MYjaeDiKHgpmFRAtpks9CpOuqkX-g_2888|date=21 June 2024}}) within this page, which includes codes assigned by the Ministry of the Interior as well as political parties and alliances (New Popular Front and Ensemble) as analysed by ''Le Monde'' for all 4,010 candidates.</ref>

Due to the suddenness of the [[Dissolution of parliament#France|dissolution]] of the [[National Assembly (France)|National Assembly]], significantly fewer candidates ran in the legislative elections in 2024 as compared to previous years, with only 4,010 candidates in 577 constituencies (the lowest figure since the [[1988 French legislative election|1988 election]]). The decline was also due to both national and local alliances. Smaller parties – such as the [[Animalist Party]], which presented 421 candidates and received 1.1% of the vote in 2022 but announced it would not present candidates in 2024 – were the most significantly affected due to their inability to negotiate alliances with larger parties and present candidates in the majority of constituencies with such short notice.<ref name="PA">{{cite news|last1=Durand|first1=Mathilde|title=Législatives anticipées : pourquoi beaucoup moins de candidats se présentent par rapport à 2022|url=https://www.leparisien.fr/elections/legislatives/legislatives-anticipees-pourquoi-beaucoup-moins-de-candidats-se-presentent-par-rapport-a-2022-19-06-2024-NMLGSOH3EFEIXCYYS574AASB2Q.php|access-date=21 June 2024|work=Le Parisien|date=19 June 2024|archive-date=21 June 2024|archive-url=https://web.archive.org/web/20240621081653/https://www.leparisien.fr/elections/legislatives/legislatives-anticipees-pourquoi-beaucoup-moins-de-candidats-se-presentent-par-rapport-a-2022-19-06-2024-NMLGSOH3EFEIXCYYS574AASB2Q.php|url-status=live}}</ref><ref name="LM1"/>
